<div id="review_670808783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670808783" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670808783?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Regina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=arc-publisher-netgalley-edelweiss">arc-publisher-netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670808783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12033718142465537828">The world of dystopia young adult fiction is pretty crowded right now. It is the what is the what in genre fiction. Given that, it is hard to find a book that is fresh and provides a perspective not yet covered by all of the post-apocalypse/dystopia books out there – it is pretty exciting to find one that is new. Not a Drop to Drink is that fresh perspective. <br/><br/>The book starts from the improbable premise of a young girl who is around the age of 16 and only knows one person in the world – her mothe</span>
  <span id="freeText12033718142465537828" style="display:none">The world of dystopia young adult fiction is pretty crowded right now. It is the what is the what in genre fiction. Given that, it is hard to find a book that is fresh and provides a perspective not yet covered by all of the post-apocalypse/dystopia books out there – it is pretty exciting to find one that is new. Not a Drop to Drink is that fresh perspective. <br /><br />The book starts from the improbable premise of a young girl who is around the age of 16 and only knows one person in the world – her mother. She knows of a man who lives nearby, but doesn’t truly know him. And she knows nothing about the world but survival by offense. She spends her days either preparing for winter or protecting her water source with deadly force. <br /><br />Not a Drop to Drink takes place in a world where there was first an oil shortage and then a severe water shortage. The countryside has been abandoned by the government in the US and the cities are tightly controlled. The story takes place in rural Ohio, there is no government and daily life is more brutal than any imagined wild west or Little House on the Prairie. <br /><br />There are a lot of details about daily survival, food preparation, water purification, house building and that is what made this book interesting – and this is the part I really loved. The author realizes what it would actually take to live outside of society and the infrastructure we rely on so much. She uses those daily survival details to provide the framework of the world she builds. If readers enjoy reading about the daily details of survival then they would like this; these details are where I think the true beauty of Not a Drop to Drink is. There is great character development and a good amount of action, but what a Not a Drop to Drink demonstrates is the day to day living would be like in a post apocalyptic world. This is the Little House on the Prairie for the end of the world readers. And it is not romanticized, it is not idealistic.<br /><br />Is there romance? So what would a modern post-apoc/dystopica young adult novel be without romance – so yes, there is romance. But, romance is not the driving factor of the story and the book is not working toward a predictable happily ever after. <br /><br />In short, I loved this book. I could not put it down. It is not without flaws, but it was enjoyable and adds something new to this perhaps too full genre.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12033718142465537828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_537558786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537558786" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537558786?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537558786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1106817515826456476">Do you know how to tell if a book is beyond awesome? It will a) give you an incredibly book-hangover, b) surprise you beyond belief, and c) brutally rip your heart out. <i> Not a Drop to Drink </i> did all three. Woot. Yay. Thank you for destroying my soul. GIVE THIS BOOK 5-STARS AND A FEW AWARDS, PLEASE!!!!!!<br/><br/>I’m not exaggerating. I <i> adored </i> this book. Everything: characters, writing, plot – it exceeded everything I’d betted on. <br/><br/>For starters, I assumed this would be a journey book. I assumed the author</span>
  <span id="freeText1106817515826456476" style="display:none">Do you know how to tell if a book is beyond awesome? It will a) give you an incredibly book-hangover, b) surprise you beyond belief, and c) brutally rip your heart out. <i> Not a Drop to Drink </i> did all three. Woot. Yay. Thank you for destroying my soul. GIVE THIS BOOK 5-STARS AND A FEW AWARDS, PLEASE!!!!!!<br><br>I’m not exaggerating. I <i> adored </i> this book. Everything: characters, writing, plot – it exceeded everything I’d betted on. <br><br>For starters, I assumed this would be a journey book. I assumed the author would fling Lynn (narrator) out of her house and away from her pond and make her journey to some far off city and have an adorable romance on the way. WRONG. And, seriously, I am SO glad I was wrong. I’m doing a happy dance because I’m so glad I was wrong! I can usually predict books, and I get kind of bored. But no boredom here. I have full adoration for this book. <br><br><b> Characters? </b> I looove the characters. Lynn is tough. The phrase “tough as leather” fits her perfectly. In this post-apocalyptic world, where water is scarce, and there’s no law, she’s grown up shooting people to defend her pond. The pond keeps her and her mother alive. When you’ve lived like that ALL your life, you turn into this tough, capable person. Lynn has no compassion. No heart. HA. That’s what she leads us to believe at first. <br><br>You know what I loved about Lynn? <b> She was tough AND had a sweet side. </b> It bothers me when “strong” girls are portrayed as unfeeling and snarky, and then have to <i> change </i> throughout the book. Whaaaat? Why can’t we girls be tough and strong AND compassionate, but not have to end the book crying into boyfriend’s arms? Don’t get me wrong: I like soft girls in books as much as tough ones. But, I hate the concept of having to become “weak” (basically) in order to properly finish a book. Lynn definitely softened as the book went along. Her tongue didn’t. And her demeanor didn’t. But her heart changed. And it was beautiful. I think she was 100% beautiful the whole time, because she was bitter and loving all at once. <br><br>As for the other characters? Oh gosh, Stebbs was awesome. He oozed strength, but softness and compassion. I LOVED Lucy! She was 5-years-old and a bubbly little wisp. My only complaint is that “Lucy” and “Lynn” are so similar. Being in 3rd person, I got confused constantly reading the two names. Eli was also awesome. Romance is NOT a huge part of this book. It’s like a side-dish. Eli was sweet and musical, but tough as nails when he needed to be. And he loved fiercely. <br><br><b> The writing was blow-me-away beautiful. </b> I can’t believe how awesome it was! It was in 3rd person, which I love, but it was so intimate and focused on Lynne’s voice, it was practically in 1st. The description is bare bones. LOVE LOVE LOVE. Writing that cuts the fluff and gets down to details, sensory images, and feels-killing sentences always wins me. If I could ever write <i> half </i> as good as this, I would die happy. <br><br>I couldn’t predict it. The writing was gorgeous. The characters were breathtaking. The setting was. freaking. awesome. The ending crushed my soul like a grape…<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>I’m sorry? Did you want me to say something coherent? Forget it. THIS BOOK IS THE BEST. GO READ IT. GO READ IT NOW. THE END.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1106817515826456476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_579216071" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579216071" />
    <a title="Brandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi"><img alt="Brandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431565587p2/4765786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579216071?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandi" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi">Brandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579216071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15323578494078163876"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>Have you ever gone through a drought? Maybe had your community pass around 'drought preparedness' fliers, or had to face fines for not following a watering schedule? I have and I found it really very ulcer inducing. I remember reading about when Georgia had a really bad one several years ago that had the water shut off for certain hours, and people with a set number of gallons to use a day; I remember being so thankful that I had never been through a drought. Last summer wasn't the first </span>
  <span id="freeText15323578494078163876" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Have you ever gone through a drought? Maybe had your community pass around 'drought preparedness' fliers, or had to face fines for not following a watering schedule? I have and I found it really very ulcer inducing. I remember reading about when Georgia had a really bad one several years ago that had the water shut off for certain hours, and people with a set number of gallons to use a day; I remember being so thankful that I had never been through a drought. Last summer wasn't the first drought I've been through since then, but when we had a drought here in upstate New York I was caught completely off guard, and my anxiety went through the roof! I had thought a place like this wasn't in danger of all that really, but times, they are a-changin. My point with this back story is that I've always been very anxious about water, and reading stories like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13112869.Not_a_Drop_to_Drink_" title="Not a Drop to Drink  by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">Not a Drop to Drink</a> really stoke that fear.<br><br><b>
  <i>The only water she'd ever known was laced with dirt and tasted slightly of fish.</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>..."life was falling from the sky."</i>
</b><br><br>The story is about two women, a mother and daughter, who for the last 16 years have perfected the art of survival. Lynn's mother is <i>hard</i>; she has become a killer in order to secure the only reliable water source available to her and her only child, and taught Lynn to be just as hard. <b>"Lynn was nine the first time she killed..." "Death and gun powder were scents from her childhood..."</b><br><br>Then one day everything changes when Lynn no longer has her mother for protection, and she ends up not only forming an uneasy friendship with her only neighbor, but she actually takes on a dying little girl she found in the woods. Lynn had only ever had her mother, but when she finds Lucy, and the others with her, suddenly she realizes that you can help people without compromising your own safety. <br><br>The only thing I will say that I wasn't happy with was having the back story for <i>why</i> there was a water shortage be so late in the book. This could just be a personal issue, because there are hints leading up to the why of it, but I prefer to know earlier than later. <br><br>I really loved the prose and the way that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5351825.Mindy_McGinnis" title="Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">Mindy McGinnis</a> cultivated a sense of desperation and loneliness without ever going over the top for the sake of it. She created a situation that was believable, and characters that work their way into your heart. I highly recommend this book to anyone who likes survival stories, strong female characters, and realism.<br><br> <br><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15323578494078163876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1468250378" />
    <a title="Kylie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30403153-kylie"><img alt="Kylie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583675812p2/30403153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1468250378?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kylie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kylie" href="/user/show/30403153-kylie">Kylie</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468250378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13143971741396955566">Post Apocalyptic / Apocalypse books are my first love (followed by phycological thrillers) but I find myself 90% of the time skimming over the violence and fight/action chapters because they feel never ending and repetitive.<br/><br/>This book however was such a beautiful surprise! I loved it! I love the way the author wrote. You do not need an action movie in a book to make a lasting impact.</span>

<div id="review_692333779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/692333779" />
    <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales"><img alt="Dark Faerie Tales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253675501p2/2766672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/692333779?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark Faerie Tales" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales">Dark Faerie Tales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2766672-dark-faerie-tales?shelf=reviewed-by-bridget">reviewed-by-bridget</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer692333779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3078869150406194691">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales.<br/><br/>Quick & Dirty: Beautiful, realistic, and heartbreaking story about love, friendship, and survival. With a wonderful cast of characters and a very unique idea, Not a Drop to Drink is an unforgettable story that all fans of dystopian/post-apocalyptic books should read.<br/><br/>Opening Sentence: Lynn was nine the first time she killed to defend the pond, the sweet smell of water luring the man to be picked off like the barn swallows that dared to swoop in for a drink.<br/><br/>The</span>
  <span id="freeText3078869150406194691" style="display:none">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales.<br /><br />Quick &amp; Dirty: Beautiful, realistic, and heartbreaking story about love, friendship, and survival. With a wonderful cast of characters and a very unique idea, Not a Drop to Drink is an unforgettable story that all fans of dystopian/post-apocalyptic books should read.<br /><br />Opening Sentence: Lynn was nine the first time she killed to defend the pond, the sweet smell of water luring the man to be picked off like the barn swallows that dared to swoop in for a drink.<br /><br />The Review:<br /><br />The story is set in the future and most of the world’s water supply has run out. At first there was just a drought, then much of the water got contaminated and was no longer safe to drink. Now most of the population lives in a city with very strict reproduction laws, and very little room to live. But if you were lucky and had a water supply, you could live outside the city. It’s not an easy life because there are others who will try to take what little you have, but you are free and safe from the abuse and disease that runs wild in the cities.<br /><br />Lynn is 16 years old and lives with her mother outside the city. They have a small pond on their property that they have spent most of their lives protecting. They live in the basement of her mother’s childhood home where it is easy to defend from intruders. Lynn’s mother has taught her how to survive and when it comes to any strangers, it’s shoot first and ask questions later. Then one fateful day there is a terrible accident and Lynn’s mother is killed. Now Lynn is all alone and she was never prepared to live by herself, she didn’t realize it would be so lonely. She was taught to be ruthless and to trust no one, but she soon realizes that not everything her mother taught her was always right. Some people have bad intentions but there are also good people in the world as well. Soon she meets some unexpected people and she decides to open her home to them and eventually her heart.<br /><br />I loved Lynn, she is an amazing character with so many wonderful qualities. She has a very strong presence, and while she is rough around the edges, she is actually very likeable. For most of her life she never was allowed to show compassion, but when her mother passes she is forced to venture out of her comfort zone. It is a struggle for her to open up and trust others, but as she does you get to see the real Lynn. Yes, she has a very tough side and she’s not afraid to fight for what is hers, but she also has a very gentle sweet side as well. You get to experience so many firsts with Lynn which made your connection with her even stronger. She is a character that has a lot of depth and I couldn’t help but love her.<br /><br />This was an amazingly realistic story of survival. The idea was so unique and it was written beautifully. It was full of hope, love, friendship, and heartbreak. There were moments the made me laugh, moments that made my heart melt, and moments where I cried. It pulled out so many emotions that made me deeply connect with the story. The book flowed perfectly and the plot had some pretty surprising twists. There were parts of the story that I didn’t love, but I felt that if it had turned out differently it wouldn’t have felt as authentic and real. So while I wish some things would have been different, I think that the ending fit the story perfectly. Overall, I really enjoyed this book and would highly recommend it to anyone that’s a fan of dystopian or post-apocalyptic books.<br /><br />Notable Scene:<br /><br />“Shush,” Mother said. “Listen.”<br /><br />The lights didn’t move, and the utter silence of the night overwhelmed<br /><br />Lynn. Even though it was cool, she swiped a bead of sweat that rolled down her nose. A stunned cricket tentatively renewed its song, to be answered by another a second later. Soon a chorus had begun. The lights still didn’t move.<br /><br />“Think they gave up?”<br /><br />“No,” Mother said tightly. “Be quiet.”<br /><br />The lights remained still, but the crickets stopped.<br /><br />“Here they come,” Mother said confidently, cocking her weapon. “Aim at what you hear. They dropped their lights.”<br /><br />The rustling sounds of field grass followed moments later, and Lynn fired toward it. The scuffling stopped, but another sound followed, a low moan that could only mean she’d hit her target. More silence ensued. A male voice cut through the night, a sound so alien to Lynn that she cringed.<br /><br />“Come on down now, girlies. We know you’re up there,” he shouted, his voice much nearer than expected.<br /><br />“And now I know where you are, you stupid son of a—” Mother used a word that Lynn had never heard before, and fired her weapon once. The sound of a body slumping to the ground followed. Minutes passed with nothing but the continuous low groan of the man Lynn had wounded.<br /><br />“What’s that word you said?” Lynn asked, curiosity getting the best of her.<br /><br />“Never mind that now.”<br /><br />A cricket chirped and the wounded man cried out again, silencing it.<br /><br />Lynn thought she heard movement farther out from the house, and Mother’s taut body reflected that she heard it too. It faded, and they sat tensely together for nearly an hour, hearing nothing but the occasional complaint from the wounded man.<br /><br />“I think they’re gone,” Lynn said.<br /><br />“Yeah,” Mother agreed, her eyes still scanning the darkness futilely.<br /><br />“We’ll stay up on the roof, go down in the morning, get those flashlights.<br /><br />They’ll come in handy.”<br /><br />Another low moan rose from the grass. “That was a good shot,” Mother said, nodding toward it.<br /><br />“Not good enough.”<br /><br />Mother shrugged. “It was dark.” She rose and stretched out her stiff body, a sign that she truly felt safe. “You’ll get better.”<br /><br />Another cry. Mother licked her finger, tested the wind, and fired once into the night.<br /><br />Silence fell.<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Katherine Tegen Books/Harper Collins provided me with a copy of Not a Drop to Drink. No goody bags, sponsorships, “material connections,” or bribes were exchanged for my review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3078869150406194691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_671322152" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/671322152" />
    <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland"><img alt="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417030210p2/5749698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/671322152?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland">Kat (Lost in Neverland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=bloody-brilliant">bloody-brilliant</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=awesome-cover">awesome-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=blew-me-away">blew-me-away</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer671322152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8239903056820983300"><br/>OH<br/>OHH<br/>OHHHHHH<br/><br/>I FEEL LIKE I JUST HAD AN ORGASM.<br/><br/>OH THAT WAS GOOD. <br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386885012ra/7473014.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>REVIEW TO COME. <s> no pun intended, oh god</s><br/><br/>Lynn and her mother live in a world where water is a precious resource. Together, they watch over their pond from thirsty scavengers, shooting them down whether they're human or animal. <br/><br/>A tragic accident leaves Lynn on her own for the first time in her life. She must protect the pond from the dangers in the South and the threat of a new family living by the stream nearby. <br/>In a world not far fro</span>
  <span id="freeText8239903056820983300" style="display:none"><br>OH<br>OHH<br>OHHHHHH<br><br>I FEEL LIKE I JUST HAD AN ORGASM.<br><br>OH THAT WAS GOOD. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386885012ra/7473014.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>REVIEW TO COME. <s> no pun intended, oh god</s><br><br>Lynn and her mother live in a world where water is a precious resource. Together, they watch over their pond from thirsty scavengers, shooting them down whether they're human or animal. <br><br>A tragic accident leaves Lynn on her own for the first time in her life. She must protect the pond from the dangers in the South and the threat of a new family living by the stream nearby. <br>In a world not far from our own, McGinnis weaves a story that instantly draws you in with simple writing that flowed over the page. <br><br>The ending was absolute perfection and that's probably why I'm ignoring some of the issues I had with the rest of the story. <br><br>Extremely likeable characters and sudden plot twists keep you reading with intrigue. <br>Lynn is someone you would not want to fuck with if you ever came across her. Her mother raised her to be a killer and that's ultimately what she grows up to be, and a badass one. <br><br>Stebbs is one of the quiet but loveable characters that you can't help but like. I would go into other characters but I'm not sure if they would count as spoilers or not. <br><br>A couple problems I'd like to put out there; <br>I found it really unrealistic that Lynn's mother never told her what sex was. <br>Sure, she's never seen a man besides Stebbs and the ones she kills in her life, but what if she got caught by one of the men from the South? She wouldn't even know what was happening to her. <br>I would think, since her mother distrusts men so much, she'd make sure to tell Lynn what happens and what they are capable of. That whole bit with Lynn being 17 years old and not knowing what sex was is very fishy, and seriously unrealistic. <br>I thought it was one of those stupid YA novel things, where the girl has to be 'naive' and 'innocent' regarding sex and blushing at those kinds of things. <br>I'm so sick of seeing that. Can we have girl characters that openly discuss sex without blushing or being regarded as the 'sluts' of the book? <br>Just, fucking hell. <br><br>The lead-up to the ending was a bit too quick for my taste. This is the one part that I would have actually liked it to be drawn out and more dramatic. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The little bits where Lynn would worry about Eli having 'sexytimes' with Neva were absolutely ridiculous. Neva, for one, was his brother's widowed wife, and wayyyy too old for him. Plus, she had just had a stillborn baby and was raped who knows how many times when they were taken by the soldiers. I highly doubt she'd be mentally and physically able for sexytimes with a 16 year old boy. For god's sakes, Lynn.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Other than those few points, I really loved this book. It took gender roles and fucked them in the ass, making the female character the badass fighter while making the male love interest, to be honest, useless and what-how-does-a-gun-work-derp character. That's usually the girl in that position and I'm so glad it was switched around for once. <s>Even though I did find the romance between Lynn and the love interest severely forced.</s> <br><br>Finally, someone who can accurately write about a realistic post-apocalyptic/other world novel without all the 'love conquers all' crap (looking at you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14290364.Champion__Legend___3_" title="Champion (Legend, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Champion</a> ). <br><br>Unique, brilliantly executed, and simply fantastic, I'm hoping McGinnis will come out with more books in the future and possibly even a sequel to this one. <br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8239903056820983300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349628433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer276944043958996575">This was a great, yet sad, character driven book. There is very little fast paced action, yet I found the story very immersive. The events and the water-deficient world created were, unfortunately, highly believable. Overall, a contemplative and somber look at what our world could be facing down the road.</span>

<div id="review_543778050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543778050" />
    <a title="Celeste_pewter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16386248-celeste-pewter"><img alt="Celeste_pewter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482736744p2/16386248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/543778050?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste_pewter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste_pewter" href="/user/show/16386248-celeste-pewter">Celeste_pewter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer543778050&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543778050" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17962466999209097716"><b>Two-second recap:</b> In Not a Drop to Drink, Mindy McGinnis taps into a very fundamental part of the human psyche - the need to survive against all odds. Through her deft writing style and expert plotting, readers will develop a strong kinship for Lynn and her motley band of survivors, as they battle for their survival. <br/><br/>***<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>There are times when I'll read a book and I think: This book is destined to become a classic. This is the type of book that teachers will put into the hands of their </span>
  <span id="freeText17962466999209097716" style="display:none"><b>Two-second recap:</b> In Not a Drop to Drink, Mindy McGinnis taps into a very fundamental part of the human psyche - the need to survive against all odds. Through her deft writing style and expert plotting, readers will develop a strong kinship for Lynn and her motley band of survivors, as they battle for their survival. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />There are times when I'll read a book and I think: This book is destined to become a classic. This is the type of book that teachers will put into the hands of their students, intriguing and inspiring future students. I definitely felt like this with Robyn Schneider's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13522285.The_Beginning_of_Everything" title="The Beginning of Everything by Robyn Schneider" rel="nofollow noopener">The Beginning of Everything</a>, and I absolutely feel this way about <i>Not A Drop to Drink.</i><br /><br />This is a book that's very different from the other dystopians currently out there, and I genuinely believe that this book is destined to sit on bookshelves everywhere, next to books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5148.A_Separate_Peace" title="A Separate Peace by John Knowles" rel="nofollow noopener">A Separate Peace</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64316.The_White_Mountains__The_Tripods___1_" title="The White Mountains (The Tripods, #1) by John Christopher" rel="nofollow noopener">The White Mountains</a>.<br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>Plot overview:</b> (Keeping this vague, since I want others to surprised!)<br /><br />For most of her life, Lynn and Mother have lived to protect their own corner of the world. Their entire livelihood has depending on defending their home, and the pond next to their home. <br /><br />Lynn's more or less happy with the way of life that she's been taught by Mother - focusing only on the essentials - and focusing instead on their constant struggle to survive. <br /><br />However, a series of events eventually challenges both Lynn's way of life and her worldview, leaving her to rebuild her understanding of almost everything around her, from the ground up. <br /><br /><br />***<br /><br />Things that worked:<br /><br />* The writing. <br /><br />McGinnis writes with the confidence and ease of an accomplished writer. She also makes the interesting decision of writing in third-person, past tense. Without getting too overly analytical, I think this opens up the narrative in a way, which wouldn't have happened had it been in first-person or present tense. We're not constantly spending time in Lynn's head, alone with her thoughts and it makes it easier to sympathize with the situation.<br /><br />* Characterizations<br /><br />I think the best way to describe the way that McGinnis builds her characters, is to compare them to a Jackson Pollock painting. Picture the splashes of paint that Pollock throws onto his work. They're violent and stark, but still extremely beautiful to the human eye. That's exactly how McGinnis's characters appeared to me.<br /><br />All of the characters - Mother especially - are very stark, but they also have a hidden beauty and strength. It was extremely rewarding for me to watch Lynn find her own inner strength, and begin to trust others and also realize that there can be a life beyond just the nearby fields and forest. <br /><br />Similarly, I loved seeing other characters finding their own personal strength in different ways - whether it was Stebb's ability to encourage kindness out of others, or Eli finding his physical strength. <br /><br />Also, something to consider about the characterization: <br /><br />McGinnis's story unfolds in a way in which you do get to know the characters, but not in a way in which you'd get to know them in a traditional format. <br /><br />While you do learn small things about the characters - e.g. Lynn knows (somewhat obscure) poetry because of all of the books that Mother has stockpiled around the house, she doesn't know what electricity-lit homes looks like - the primary focus of the book is always on how they react to the constant hunt for water and resources. McGinnis's approach reminded me of the storytelling on <i>The Walking Dead</i> in a way, and I thought it was an interesting (and the right!) choice for her to make. <br /><br />* The world-building. <br /><br />Unlike other books, the world-building in the book isn't overly detailed. We're given strong explanations for how the world ended up the way it ended up, but it's McGinnis definitely doesn't make it a point to offer the small details that you might find in other books. <br /><br />Again, I think this is a very specific choice by McGinnis that works - she's essentially encouraging us to concentrate solely on the setting of the story, and Lynn's key points of residence and surrounding areas, specifically. <br /><br />And while I hate to keep bringing up the <i>The Walking Dead</i>, but McGinnis method is very similar to how they focus on very specific settings on the show - e.g. the prison. <br /><br /><br />* Plotting<br /><br />McGinnis keeps the plot moving along at a brisk pace. There aren't any of the usual dramatic!explosions!mass deaths! that you might find in a typical dystopian, and the book is all the stronger for it. Instead, the shocking moments are very human-driven. Ultimately, I think this adds more heart and impact for the story that McGinnis is telling. <br /><br /><br />* Finally,<br /><br />The cover. It's beautiful, intriguing and eye-catching. A huge bravo to the cover designers at Harpers/Katherine Tegen books. <br /><br />(Suggestion though: for more popular advertising, maybe advertise the book to younger fans of The Walking Dead? I think that the book will definitely appeal to those fans.)<br /><br /><br />***<br /><br />Things that didn't work/Things to consider:<br /><br />*SPOILERS!*<br /><br /><br /><br />The only thing that I would have been interested in having McGinnis do differently, is to not have such a significant time jump between the final chapter and the epilogue. <br /><br />So much of the book is about Lynn coming to terms with the fact that she no longer has to isolate herself from others, and it's okay to become a part of a community. <br /><br />While Lynn does get to be a part of that community in the epilogue, I think it would have added to the story if we had seen more of the transitional period that she obviously experiences between the last chapter and the epilogue. However, just my opinion! <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>Final verdict:</b> Not a Drop to Drink is unlike most of the current dystopians/speculative fiction books. I highly recommend this book for all readers, especially those interested in books with strong female protagonists. <br /><br /><b>Disclaimer:</b> I received an ARC of Not A Drop to Drink from HarperCollins via Edelweiss, in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17962466999209097716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_587974620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/587974620" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/587974620?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17376283-not-a-drop-to-drink">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=arcs-edelweiss">arcs-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587974620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2948375175347147580">My rating: 3.5 of 5 stars<br/>A copy of Not a Drop to Drink was provided to me by Katherine Tegen Books for review purposes.<br/><br/>Seeing that my one of my favorite genres is dystopian/post-apocalyptic, this was high on my expectations list. Post-apocalyptic became super popular in recent years and practically all the ways the world could possibly come to an end have been covered. A world where the water has been contaminated and clean water is a precious commodity? I had yet to read a book covering that so</span>
  <span id="freeText2948375175347147580" style="display:none">My rating: 3.5 of 5 stars<br />A copy of Not a Drop to Drink was provided to me by Katherine Tegen Books for review purposes.<br /><br />Seeing that my one of my favorite genres is dystopian/post-apocalyptic, this was high on my expectations list. Post-apocalyptic became super popular in recent years and practically all the ways the world could possibly come to an end have been covered. A world where the water has been contaminated and clean water is a precious commodity? I had yet to read a book covering that so I eagerly awaited this one.<br /><br />The story starts off strong, introducing Lynn and her mother, a duo that has learned to survive on their own in the harsh world. For years it's just been the two of them protecting the pond that gives them the only hope of living to see another day. The day to day accounting of the daily tasks they performed in order to survive were detailed and authentic. As the book progresses, we're given vague details regarding how the world came to be and while it was enough to paint an adequate picture it wasn't sufficient enough to appease my curiosity of this harsh world.<br /><br />The writing is bleak and subtle, but albeit fitting. It properly depicts a world that we could only dream of; a world where turning on your faucet to get water is no longer a reality. Lynn is the definition of strength and is willing and able to do whatever needs to be done to protect the pond. She reminded me of the character Ree from Winter's Bone by Daniel Woodrell, another literary figure that was burdened with great responsibility at a young age. Lynn grew up solely with her mother, only seeing glimpses of a single neighbor, and seeing any others through the cross-hairs of her rifle before she took them down. There was no guilt or remorse for those acts, she was simply doing what needed to be done to secure her own personal survival. She was a solid character during the first 1/3 or so of the novel but I had issue with how she changed as the book progressed. <br /><br />Without giving too many details as most are potential spoilers, more characters are introduced and a romance even develops. Considering the ways that Lynn was raised, being completely unaccustomed to social skills or people in general, the fact that a romance was introduced seemed too far fetched. Personally I felt that her willingness to let people into her life and building trust was difficult enough to incorporate into what we already knew of her as a character, but a romance was simply unnecessary.<br /><br />Books that I feel are most similar are: Ashfall, The Road, and Orleans so if you're fans of those you should consider checking this out. If you're looking for an action-packed adventure, this isn't it. Not a Drop to Drink is a story that slowly builds with intensity and is predominantly a story of surviving in a harsh and grim world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2948375175347147580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_537132545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537132545" />
    <a title="Kassidy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy"><img alt="Kassidy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585073850p2/8937622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537132545?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kassidy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kassidy" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy">Kassidy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537132545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10088842766348418907">*4.5*<br/><br/>I loved this so much!! Don't go into this thinking it's going to be action from the first page because it's not. It is slow and focuses on characters, but that is what I loved about this book. It definitely reminds me of the show The Walking Dead, but without zombies. It is about people and how they are surviving in this deteriorating world. I adored all of the characters, especially the main character Lynn. I love how they all come from different walks of life, but they ban together to mak</span>
  <span id="freeText10088842766348418907" style="display:none">*4.5*<br /><br />I loved this so much!! Don't go into this thinking it's going to be action from the first page because it's not. It is slow and focuses on characters, but that is what I loved about this book. It definitely reminds me of the show The Walking Dead, but without zombies. It is about people and how they are surviving in this deteriorating world. I adored all of the characters, especially the main character Lynn. I love how they all come from different walks of life, but they ban together to make the best of their situation. <br />Lynn is so great and such an interesting character. She has lived in the wilderness all her life and has never even experienced electricity. She's shot a gun since she was strong enough to hold one, and all she has lived for is survival and staying alive day to day. Her life changes in this book and it was wonderful seeing her grow, learn, and experience what it means to live.<br />This is a wonderful, realistic survival story that definitely does not skimp out on the hard ships of a world that is being depleted of water.<br /><br />My only problem with this book is that I wanted MORE, it was too short haha <br />I wanted further insight into characters and relationships, I wanted a better idea of the world as a whole, and I want to know more about why all of this is happening. Maybe that will be further explored in the sequel coming out this year ;)<br /><br />Great read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10088842766348418907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004521003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10833414936181477005">*4.5 stars*<br/><br/>Trigger warning for rape and sex slavery. <br/><br/>Lynn has never had a normal life. In this post-apocalyptic world, "normal" can vary widely, but Lynn's mother taught her to survive and to never let her guard down. But when Lynn's mother dies, Lynn is suddenly thrust into circumstances she'd never experienced before. Her closest neighbor, Stubbs, introduces her to a family living at a nearby stream. Newly escaped from the city, they're starving and unable to take care of themselves. Lynn know</span>
  <span id="freeText10833414936181477005" style="display:none">*4.5 stars*<br /><br />Trigger warning for rape and sex slavery. <br /><br />Lynn has never had a normal life. In this post-apocalyptic world, "normal" can vary widely, but Lynn's mother taught her to survive and to never let her guard down. But when Lynn's mother dies, Lynn is suddenly thrust into circumstances she'd never experienced before. Her closest neighbor, Stubbs, introduces her to a family living at a nearby stream. Newly escaped from the city, they're starving and unable to take care of themselves. Lynn knows what choice her mother would have made, but her heart is telling her to do things differently. <br /><br />In some ways, this novel reminds me of Rae Carson's "Walk on Earth a Stranger." Both feature tough teenage protagonists in unforgiving landscapes. In "Not a Drop to Drink," however, I was disappointed in certain elements of the ending. I also felt the epilogue was anti-climatic, and wanted to know exactly how many years had elapsed. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y1r/Eg4K3NUWbfMj95c2bDUP3Lq/uOrCPa8+qTDdWWwIKLPMjt6b1PmB+j9Gs47OVYJkWgIjHYzXBigsqu1dog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/jGSfJAIPXqaFN2KvRc8hlH0CP0prQjSwOjT29bDxDg9Q96iENx6e3X41JYMM4QkMXmwHZQ2/5wqQcVeTPPA9g==')})
  }
